2:20:1030:0:14:72:329:700:12:Times:12:Times:C:The Effect of Depression on Labor Market Outcomes
2:21:1079:14:14:72:371:686:12:Times:12:Times:C:Lizhong Peng, Chad D. Meyerhoefer, and Samuel H. Zuvekas
2:22:1135:14:14:72:234:672:12:Times:12:Times:C:NBER Working Paper No. 19451
2:23:1163:14:14:72:150:658:12:Times:12:Times:C:September 2013
2:24:1177:14:28:72:174:644:12:Times:12:Times:C:JEL No. C23,I10,J22
2:25:1196:28:28:306:339:616:12:Times:12:Times:C:ABSTRACT
2:26:1204:28:14:72:540:588:12:Times:12:Times:C:We estimated the effect of depression on labor market outcomes using data from the 2004-2009 Medical
2:27:1304:14:14:72:540:574:12:Times:12:Times:C:Expenditure Panel Survey.  After accounting for the endogeneity of depression through a correlated
2:28:1402:14:14:72:540:560:12:Times:12:Times:C:random effects panel data specification, we found that depression reduces the likelihood of employment.
2:29:1505:14:14:72:540:546:12:Times:12:Times:C:We did not, however, find evidence of a causal relationship between depression and hourly wages
2:30:1600:14:14:72:540:532:12:Times:12:Times:C:or weekly hours worked. Our estimates are substantially smaller than those from previous studies,
2:31:1697:14:14:72:540:518:12:Times:12:Times:C:and imply that depression reduces the probability of employment by 2.6 percentage points. In addition,
2:32:1799:14:14:72:540:504:12:Times:12:Times:C:we examined the effect of depression on work impairment and found that depression increases annual
2:33:1897:14:14:72:540:490:12:Times:12:Times:C:work loss days by about 1.4 days (33 percent), which implies that the annual aggregate productivity
2:34:1996:14:42:72:540:476:12:Times:12:Times:C:loses due to depression-induced absenteeism range from $700 million to 1.4 billion in 2009 USD.
2:35:2091:42:14:72:139:434:12:Times:12:Times:C:Lizhong Peng
2:36:2103:14:14:72:201:420:12:Times:12:Times:C:Department of Economics,
2:37:2127:14:14:72:160:406:12:Times:12:Times:C:Lehigh University
2:38:2144:14:28:72:164:392:12:Times:12:Times:C:lip210@lehigh.edu
2:39:2161:28:14:72:177:364:12:Times:12:Times:C:Chad D. Meyerhoefer
2:40:2180:14:14:72:183:350:12:Times:12:Times:C:Rauch Business Center
2:41:2201:14:14:72:160:336:12:Times:12:Times:C:Lehigh University
2:42:2218:14:14:72:156:322:12:Times:12:Times:C:621 Taylor Street
2:43:2235:14:14:72:178:308:12:Times:12:Times:C:Bethlehem, PA 18015
2:44:2254:14:14:72:124:294:12:Times:12:Times:C:and NBER
2:45:2262:14:0:72:172:280:12:Times:12:Times:C:chm308@lehigh.edu
2:46:2279:0:14:306:400:434:12:Times:12:Times:C:Samuel H. Zuvekas
2:47:2296:14:14:306:528:420:12:Times:12:Times:C:Center for Financing, Access and Cost Trends
2:48:2340:14:14:306:522:406:12:Times:12:Times:C:Agency for Healthcare Research and Quality
2:49:2382:14:14:306:391:392:12:Times:12:Times:C:540 Gaither Road
2:50:2398:14:14:306:411:378:12:Times:12:Times:C:Rockville, MD 20850
2:51:2417:14:0:306:455:364:12:Times:12:Times:C:samuel.zuvekas@ahrq.hhs.gov
3:52:2445:0:26:90:163:709:11:Times New Roman:11:Times New Roman:F:1. Introduction 
3:53:2460:26:27:90:502:683:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:Mental health problems are prevalent among U.S. adults. It is estimated that about 26 
3:54:2545:27:28:90:521:656:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:percent of adults have some type of mental disorder broadly defined, and 6 percent suffer 
3:55:2633:28:27:90:517:628:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:from severe mental illness (Kessler et al, 2005). The costs associated with mental illness 
3:56:2719:27:28:90:516:601:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:include direct medical costs for mental health treatment and indirect costs in the form of 
3:57:2809:28:28:90:458:573:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:time away from work (absenteeism) and reduced productivity while at work 
3:58:2882:28:27:90:514:545:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:(presenteeism). The National Institute of Mental Health (NIMH) estimated that the total 
3:59:2968:27:28:90:508:518:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:annual cost for people with severely debilitating mental disorders exceeds $300 billion 
3:60:3053:28:27:90:504:490:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:each year, a large fraction of which falls on payers of medical services and employers 
3:61:3138:27:28:90:168:463:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:(NIMH, 2002).  
3:62:3151:28:28:126:524:435:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:A:Among various mental health conditions, depression is of interest for two reasons. 
3:63:3231:28:27:90:508:407:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:First, it is one of the most common mental health problems among adults. In 2011, 6.6 
3:64:3312:27:28:90:511:380:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:percent of adults aged 18 or older in the U.S. (15.2 million people) experienced at least 
3:65:3398:28:27:90:502:352:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:one major depressive episode during the past year (National Survey on Drug Use and 
3:66:3480:27:28:90:516:325:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:Health, 2011). Second, the social cost of depression is surprisingly high: in high-income 
3:67:3566:28:28:90:483:297:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:countries, unipolar depression (also known as major depressive disorder or major 
3:68:3646:28:27:90:521:269:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:depression) is the leading cause of burden of disease and accounts for 8.2 percent of total 
3:69:3735:27:28:90:506:242:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:disability-adjusted life years (DALYs). In contrast, heart diseases only account for 6.3 
3:70:3822:28:27:90:279:214:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:percent of total DALYs (WHO, 2008). 
3:71:3856:27:28:126:497:187:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:A:A correct understanding of the economic costs associated with mental health 
3:72:3930:28:28:90:506:159:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:problems has important policy implications. Historically, mental health conditions are 
3:73:4017:28:0:90:520:131:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:covered less generously than physical illness by private insurance, which has contributed 
4:74:4105:0:28:90:509:709:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:to under-treatment of mental health problems.1 Legislators at both the federal and state 
4:75:4191:28:28:90:506:681:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:level responded by enacting mental health parity laws that aim to expand coverage for 
4:76:4273:28:27:90:517:653:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:mental health conditions. However, it is still unclear whether these parity laws influence 
4:77:4363:27:28:90:519:626:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:health outcomes (GAO, 2011), and if mental health conditions do not significantly affect 
4:78:4450:28:27:90:522:598:12:g_d0_f4:12:Times New Roman:B:individuals’ labor market opportunities, the benefits of expanding mental health coverage 
4:79:4539:27:28:90:198:571:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:may justify the costs.  
4:80:4562:28:28:126:523:543:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:A:There is a well-documented cross-sectional association in the economics literature 
4:81:4639:28:27:90:504:515:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:between poor mental health and reduced likelihood of employment, lower wages, and 
4:82:4720:27:28:90:510:488:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:fewer hours worked. Mental disorders are characterized by poor concentration, fatigue, 
4:83:4804:28:27:90:509:460:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:sadness, reduced cognitive ability, excessive guilt, or even thoughts of suicide (NIMH, 
4:84:4890:27:28:90:481:433:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:2011). These symptoms reduce human capital accumulation, which in turn limits 
4:85:4967:28:28:90:518:405:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:potential wages and the benefits of participating in the formal labor market. (Ettner et al, 
4:86:5059:28:27:90:513:377:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:1997). Among the employed, the onset of symptoms can result in absenteeism (absence 
4:87:5141:27:28:90:520:350:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:from work) and presenteeism (attending work while sick). Furthermore, when employers 
4:88:5223:28:27:90:507:322:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:learn an individual has a mental health condition they are sometimes less likely to hire 
4:89:5310:27:28:90:524:295:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:him due to the inability or unwillingness to provide needed accommodations, or they may 
4:90:5395:28:28:90:393:267:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:even engage in outright discrimination. (Chatterji et al, 2011).  
4:91:5458:28:27:126:513:239:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:A:The main difficulty in attributing poor labor market outcomes to the presence of 
4:92:5538:27:28:90:524:212:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:mental health problems in a cross section of individuals is endogeneity. As pointed out by 
4:93:5629:28:27:90:479:184:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:Chatterji et al (2011), mental health status is endogenous in both a structural and 
4:94:5710:27:28:90:499:157:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:statistical sense: reverse causality poses a threat to identification if mental health and 
4:95:5800:28:26:90:495:129:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:labor market outcomes are determined simultaneously.  For example, job loss could 
4:96:5882:26:8:90:236:103:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:F:                                                           
4:97:5940:8:16:90:509:95:6:Times New Roman:10:Times New Roman:F:1 According to the National Survey on Drug Use and Health in 2007, among the 24.3 million adults with 
4:98:6041:16:0:90:466:79:10:Times New Roman:10:Times New Roman:F:serious psychological distress, only 44.6 percent used mental health services in the past year.  
5:99:6138:0:28:90:494:709:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:trigger an episode of depression for an individual with a predisposition. In addition, 
5:100:6224:28:28:90:503:681:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:unobserved physical and mental health status as well as unobserved productivity may 
5:101:6306:28:27:90:517:653:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:lead to omitted variable bias. In most cases, this type of endogeneity will lead to an over-
5:102:6395:27:28:90:514:626:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:estimation of the negative impact of poor mental health on labor market outcomes, such 
5:103:6482:28:27:90:494:598:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:as employment, wages, work hours and work loss days, in non-causal analyses.2 To 
5:104:6562:27:28:90:495:571:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:address this endogeneity problem, researchers have primarily relied on instrumental 
5:105:6644:28:28:90:522:543:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:variables or exclusion restrictions in multiple equation models. Nonetheless, it is difficult 
5:106:6737:28:27:90:503:515:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:to find valid instruments that affect mental health but have no impact on labor market 
5:107:6819:27:28:90:487:488:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:outcomes. The instruments that have been used in the literature fall into two broad 
5:108:6903:28:27:90:521:460:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:categories: personal characteristics and social support.3 However, the exogeneity of these 
5:109:6991:27:28:90:506:433:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:instruments is difficult to validate. For example, the same personal characteristics that 
5:110:7080:28:28:90:519:405:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:affect mental health may be correlated with productivity and labor market outcomes, and 
5:111:7167:28:27:90:514:377:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:greater support from families or communities may also be related to better labor market 
5:112:7255:27:28:90:162:350:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:opportunities.  
5:113:7269:28:27:126:489:322:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:A:We exploited the longitudinal dimension of the Medical Expenditure Panel 
5:114:7340:27:28:90:516:295:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:Survey (MEPS) to estimate the causal relationship between depression and labor market 
5:115:7425:28:28:90:488:267:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:outcomes. The MEPS is well suited to this analysis because it contains a clinically 
5:116:7509:28:27:90:510:239:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:validated measure of depression that is collected contemporaneously with several labor 
5:117:7595:27:28:90:489:212:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:market outcomes. We estimated fixed effects and correlated random effects (CRE) 
5:118:7674:28:27:90:507:184:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:models (Chamberlain, 1980), which require no exclusion restrictions for identification 
5:119:7759:27:14:90:490:157:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:and allow unobserved heterogeneity to be correlated with the regressors. This is an 
5:120:7837:14:8:90:236:143:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:F:                                                           
5:121:7895:8:18:90:522:135:6:Times New Roman:10:Times New Roman:F:2 It is possible that certain types omitted variables could result in the under-estimation of the impact of poor 
5:122:8007:18:13:90:506:117:10:Times New Roman:10:Times New Roman:F:mental health for some outcomes. For example, unobserved generosity in mental health coverage could 
5:123:8107:13:9:90:373:104:10:Times New Roman:10:Times New Roman:F:bias the effect of poor mental health towards zero in a wage equation.  
5:124:8178:9:16:90:492:95:6:Times New Roman:10:Times New Roman:F:3 See Chatterji et al (2007) for a comprehensive review of the instruments that have been used in the 
5:125:8279:16:0:90:130:79:10:Times New Roman:10:Times New Roman:F:literature. 
6:126:8291:0:28:90:499:709:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:attractive alternative method of measuring causal effects when the primary threats to 
6:127:8377:28:28:90:476:681:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:causal inference are unobservable dimensions of productivity and health status.  
6:128:8456:28:27:90:93:653:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B: 
6:129:8456:27:28:90:201:626:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:2. Literature Review  
6:130:8476:28:27:90:518:598:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:Previous research indicates that the positive relationship between poor mental health and 
6:131:8562:27:28:90:523:571:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:unemployment is strong and robust, but that the associations with wages and works hours 
6:132:8649:28:28:90:511:543:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:are less consistent, and sensitive to the type of mental disorder and modeling approach. 
6:133:8735:28:27:90:517:515:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:For example, Ettner et al. (1997) analyzed the National Co-morbidity Survey (NCS) and 
6:134:8818:27:28:90:501:488:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:found that psychiatric disorders (mainly major depression) reduced the probability of 
6:135:8899:28:27:90:487:460:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:employment by approximately 11 percentage points among both men and women. 
6:136:8971:27:28:90:492:433:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:Conditional on employment, they also found weak evidence of a small reduction in 
6:137:9048:28:28:90:504:405:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:weekly hours worked for men and a substantial reduction in income for both men and 
6:138:9129:28:27:90:502:377:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:women.  They confirmed these results using instrumental variables models where the 
6:139:9211:27:28:90:503:350:12:g_d0_f4:12:Times New Roman:B:number of psychiatric disorders of an individual’s parent and the number of disorders 
6:140:9295:28:27:90:499:322:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:diagnosed before the age of 18 were the instruments for current mental health status. 
6:141:9378:27:28:90:494:295:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:Chatterji et al (2011) used the more recent National Co-morbidity Survey-Replicate 
6:142:9458:28:28:90:524:267:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:(NCS-R) data and estimated a set of constrained bivariate probit models using the method 
6:143:9544:28:27:90:504:239:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:proposed by Altonji et al (2005). They found that past year psychiatric disorders were 
6:144:9629:27:28:90:505:212:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:associated with reductions of 9 (19) percentage points in the probability of labor force 
6:145:9716:28:27:90:501:184:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:participation and 14 (13) percentage points in the probability of employment for men 
6:146:9798:27:0:90:522:157:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:(women). However, they failed to find an effect of psychiatric disorders on hours worked 
7:147:9886:0:28:90:504:709:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:or earnings when accounting for the endogeneity of mental health status using similar 
7:148:9971:28:28:90:262:681:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:instruments to Ettner et al. (1997).4 
7:149:10008:28:27:126:515:653:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:A:There are two studies which used causal methods to investigate the labor market 
7:150:10088:27:28:90:487:626:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:consequences of depression, specifically. Alexandre and French (2001) found that 
7:151:10167:28:27:90:503:598:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:depression lead to a 19 percentage point reduction in employment and 8 fewer annual 
7:152:10247:27:28:90:508:571:12:Times New Roman:12:g_d0_f4:B:weeks worked, using instruments based on the respondent’s attitudes towards religion, 
7:153:10332:28:28:90:520:543:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:and a proxy for individual and family social support. Cseh (2008) employed fixed effects 
7:154:10419:28:27:90:497:515:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:models to account for the unobserved heterogeneity using the National Longitudinal 
7:155:10502:27:28:90:498:488:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:Survey of Youth 1979 (NLSY79). To our knowledge, this is the only study that uses 
7:156:10584:28:27:90:497:460:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:panel data techniques for identification. Relative to analyses that did not account for 
7:157:10670:27:28:90:514:433:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:endogeneity, this study found a much smaller reduction in wages for men, and no effect 
7:158:10754:28:28:90:210:405:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:on the wages of women. 
7:159:10776:28:27:126:523:377:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:A:Other studies have identified a strong association between mental health problems 
7:160:10858:27:28:90:524:350:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:and work impairment. Kessler and Frank (1997) used the NCS to demonstrate that among 
7:161:10941:28:27:90:505:322:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:the employed, individuals with psychiatric disorders in the past month had more work 
7:162:11024:27:28:90:493:295:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:loss days or work cutback days. Kessler et al. (1999) showed that past month major 
7:163:11103:28:28:90:489:267:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:depression increased short term work-disability days by 1.5 to 3.2 days per month. 
7:164:11183:28:27:90:495:239:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:Likewise, Lim et al. (2000) found that depression, anxiety disorders and personality 
7:165:11265:27:56:90:349:212:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:disorders were strong predictors of work impairment. 
7:166:11316:56:8:90:236:156:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:F:                                                           
7:167:11374:8:17:90:522:148:6:Times New Roman:10:Times New Roman:F:4 One concern with the use of instruments based on parental or past mental health status is that these factors 
7:168:11484:17:14:90:514:131:10:Times New Roman:10:Times New Roman:F:could impact current productivity through past human capital accumulation. In support of this possibility, 
7:169:11591:14:13:90:500:117:10:Times New Roman:10:Times New Roman:F:Farahati et al (2003) found that children with mentally ill parents were more likely to drop out of high 
7:170:11696:13:13:90:482:104:10:Times New Roman:10:Times New Roman:F:school, while Fletcher (2010) found that depression was associated with fewer years of schooling 
7:171:11793:13:0:90:485:91:10:Times New Roman:10:Times New Roman:F:completed, higher probability of high school dropout, and lower probability of college attendance. 
8:172:11892:0:28:126:520:709:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:A:Finally, researchers have uncovered different impacts of mental health conditions 
8:173:11972:28:28:90:505:681:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:across social groups. In particular, Chatterji et al (2007) found that poor mental health 
8:174:12060:28:27:90:498:653:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:reduced employment among Latinos as well as Asian males, but not Asians females. 
8:175:12137:27:28:90:493:626:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:Latinos were also more likely to have work absences than Asians in the presence of 
8:176:12219:28:27:90:503:598:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:psychiatric disorders and mental distress. Ojeda et al (2009) determined that the labor 
8:177:12305:27:28:90:506:571:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:supply of immigrants to the U.S. was less affected by mental health problems than the 
8:178:12387:28:28:90:208:543:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:labor supply of natives.  
8:179:12411:28:27:90:93:515:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B: 
8:180:12411:27:28:90:354:488:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:3.  Theoretical Framework and Empirical Methods 
8:181:12457:28:27:90:319:460:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:3.1 A simple theoretical model of labor supply

8:183:12583:28:40:90:383:405:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:1999). The inter-temporal utility function for individual i is

9:230:13169:66:33:90:507:603:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:The first constraint is the health production function where current health capital, itH, 
9:231:13257:33:31:90:489:570:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:depends on past health capital as well as time spent in health production, itV. i is 
9:232:13337:31:27:90:504:539:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:unobserved heterogeneity in health production. The second and third constraints are a 
9:233:13416:27:30:90:517:512:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:budget and time constraint, respectively. The budget constraint limits expenditure on the 
9:234:13506:30:35:90:521:482:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:composite commodity to no more than the sum of unearned income itA and labor income 
9:235:13587:35:30:99:513:447:7:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:A:ititQ, while the time constraint ensures that the sum of sick time, itS, hours worked, itQ
9:236:13676:30:31:90:510:417:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:, time devoted to health production, itV, and leisure, itL, equal total time available (Ω). 
9:237:13763:31:29:90:485:386:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:The fourth constraint specifies the wage is a function of health capital, a vector of 
9:238:13844:29:33:90:491:357:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:individual characteristics, itX, observed job and employer characteristics, iM, and 
9:239:13928:33:32:90:513:324:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:unobserved productivity, im. In the last constraint, sick time itS is a function of current 
9:240:14019:32:32:90:517:292:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:health capital, a vector of exogenous determinants, itZ, individual-specific propensity to 
9:241:14110:32:32:90:485:260:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:get sick, i. The individual chooses the optimal consumption path, 0itC, hours 
9:242:14189:32:32:90:501:228:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:worked, 0itQ, time inputs into health production, 0itV, to maximize his lifetime 
9:243:14272:32:39:90:469:196:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:utility subject to (3). The first-order conditions with respect to itQare given by 
9:244:14350:39:0:90:389:157:11:g_d0_f6:12:Times New Roman:B: 21,1,,   ,
9:245:14362:0:10:296:298:164:7:Times New Roman:7:Times New Roman:F:t

9:257:14480:31:0:90:262:87:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:labor supply function in period t is 
10:258:14516:0:0:90:412:704:11:g_d0_f6:12:Times New Roman:B: ,  1,,,,,.

10:261:14571:30:28:90:522:671:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:One of the distinct features of this model is that the health stock is an endogenous choice. 
10:262:14662:28:27:90:498:643:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:Individuals can affect the health stock by altering time devoted to health production. 
10:263:14746:27:28:90:512:616:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:From the quasi-reduced form equation of labor supply as a function of health, it is clear 
10:264:14836:28:27:90:460:588:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:that there are several determinants of labor supply that are unobserved to the 
10:265:14915:27:28:90:513:561:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:econometrician. Some of these, such as unobserved determinants of sickness and health 
10:266:15001:28:28:90:478:533:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:production, and unmeasured productivity have a large genetic component, while 
10:267:15077:28:27:90:519:505:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:unobserved preferences may be established prior to adulthood. Under these assumptions, 
10:268:15163:27:29:90:487:478:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:one can further decompose all the unobserved factors into time-invariant and time-
10:269:15243:29:31:90:488:449:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:varying components. Denote i and it as all the time-invariant and time-varying 
10:270:15320:31:28:90:493:418:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:determinants of labor supply, respectively, where          .  Equation (5) then 
10:271:15389:28:29:90:138:390:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:becomes: 
10:272:15397:29:30:90:525:361:12:Times New Roman:11:g_d0_f6:B:  (,,,    ,    )ititititiitQQ  X    H   M, (6) 
10:273:15443:30:28:90:337:331:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:which serves as the basis of our empirical analysis. 
10:274:15495:28:28:90:93:303:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B: 
10:275:15495:28:27:90:195:275:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:3.2 Empirical models 
10:276:15513:27:30:90:286:248:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:One basic estimating equation for (6) is: 
10:277:15552:30:32:90:525:218:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B: (),itititiitYf   XD          (7) 
10:278:15593:32:31:90:520:186:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:where itY is the labor market outcome of interest for individual i in time period t, itX is 
10:279:15680:31:30:90:501:155:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:a vector of covariates including demographics, human capital, and observed physical 
10:280:15764:30:32:90:480:125:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:health status. We use the binary indicator itD to denote whether the individual is 
10:281:15846:32:0:90:484:93:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:depressed in time period t. The time-invariant parameter i captures unobserved 
11:282:15925:0:29:90:519:709:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:components of physical and mental health status and unmeasured productivity. The error 
11:283:16011:29:32:90:508:680:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:term it is assumed to be uncorrelated with all regressors from all time periods (strong 
11:284:16096:32:31:90:524:648:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:exogeneity). The choice of ()f is dependent on the outcome itY. For employment status, 
11:285:16181:31:29:90:177:617:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:we specify (7) as  
11:286:16197:29:31:90:525:588:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B: Pr(1)(),itititiYXD             (8) 
11:287:16239:31:30:90:486:557:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:where () is the standard normal cumulative distribution function. In the case of 
11:288:16320:30:28:90:509:527:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:continuous outcomes such as hourly wage and weekly hours worked, (7) is the identity 
11:289:16403:28:27:90:522:499:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:function. Since hourly wage is highly skewed to the right, we used the log transformation 
11:290:16489:27:28:90:513:472:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:of the hourly wage as the dependent variable. In addition, we estimated a set of ordered 
11:291:16574:28:28:90:519:444:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:probit models using the conditional sample to investigate whether depression affects full-
11:292:16661:28:27:90:514:416:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:time versus part-time work status. We created three categories of weekly hours worked: 
11:293:16745:27:28:90:519:389:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:less than 30 hours a week, between 30 and 40 hours a week, and at least 40 hours a week 
11:294:16833:28:27:90:519:361:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:(full-time). The reason why we made a distinction between those who work part-time for 
11:295:16919:27:28:90:507:334:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:30 or more hours per week is that some employers offer fringe benefits (such as health 
11:296:17006:28:28:90:363:306:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:insurance) to those who work at least 30 hours a week.5  
11:297:17061:28:27:126:501:278:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:A:We are also interested in absenteeism, which is captured in the MEPS using a 
11:298:17138:27:28:90:500:251:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:count variable indicating the number work loss days during the reference period. We 
11:299:17221:28:27:90:492:223:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:modeled work loss days using the zero-inflated ordered probit (ZIOP) specification 
11:300:17303:27:28:90:505:196:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:developed by Harris and Zhao (2007). This model is more appropriate than a standard 
11:301:17386:28:28:90:491:168:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:count data model for two reasons. First, the distribution of work loss days is highly 
11:302:17470:28:20:90:518:140:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:skewed, with over 70 percent of employed individuals reporting zero work loss days and 
11:303:17554:20:8:90:236:120:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:F:                                                           
11:304:17612:8:18:90:521:112:6:Times New Roman:10:Times New Roman:F:5 According to the data from National Compensation Survey, 24 percent of the part-time workers in private 
11:305:17717:18:13:90:521:94:10:Times New Roman:10:Times New Roman:F:industry have access to medical care benefits (Employee Benefits in the United States- March 2012). URL: 
11:306:17821:13:0:90:348:81:10:Times New Roman:10:Times New Roman:F:http://www.bls.gov/news.release/archives/ebs2_07272010.pdf    
12:307:17884:0:28:90:474:709:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:only around 10 percent reporting more than 7 annual work loss days. The ZIOP 
12:308:17956:28:28:90:516:681:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:specification allowed us to account for this right skewness by combining work loss days 
12:309:18043:28:27:90:508:653:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:at the higher end of its distribution into discrete categories (Meyerhoefer and Zuvekas, 
12:310:18129:27:28:90:518:626:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:2010). Second, the ZIOP model facilitates the investigation of the effect of depression at 
12:311:18216:28:27:90:498:598:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:both the extensive and intensive margins by separately modeling two different latent 
12:312:18300:27:28:90:518:571:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:processes that generate the zero counts of work loss days. In particular, zero counts were 
12:313:18387:28:28:90:519:543:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:reported because individuals remained healthy during the sample period, or because they 
12:314:18473:28:28:90:443:515:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:did get sick, but remained at work while they were ill (i.e. presenteeism). 
12:315:18546:28:27:126:522:487:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:A:Let r be a latent variable underlying the first data generating process determining 
12:316:18628:27:29:90:142:460:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:sickness:

12:318:18678:29:30:90:512:402:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B: The individual is healthy if 0r, but when the individual becomes sick 0r. If the

13:363:20074:29:31:126:500:408:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:A:Although one could in principle model i using fixed effects, this estimation 
13:364:20151:31:28:90:507:377:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:strategy does not yield consistent parameter estimates of most nonlinear specifications 
13:365:20239:28:27:90:520:349:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:when the time series dimension of the panel is fixed (Cameron and Trivedi, 2005). As an 
13:366:20326:27:30:90:503:322:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:alternative Chamberlain (1980) proposed a random effects estimator that is consistent 
13:367:20410:30:33:90:500:292:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:when T is fixed and allows i to be correlated with all regressors in all time periods. 
13:368:20495:33:31:90:503:259:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:Again, denote (,   )XX   D and (    ,   )    , and note that ican be modeled using a 
13:369:20588:31:31:90:402:228:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:linear projection containing the regressors from all time periods: 
13:370:20653:31:33:90:525:197:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B: 1   12    2,iiiiT    TiXXXu   (14) 
13:371:20698:33:28:90:482:164:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:where iu is orthogonal to X by construction, and is assumed to be distributed as 
13:372:20773:28:8:125:133:136:7:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:A:2(0,)
13:373:20778:8:31:123:310:128:7:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:A:uN. Substituting (14) into (7), we have 
13:374:20815:31:0:90:525:97:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:F: 11(()).itiittiT    TiitYf   XXXu            (15) 
14:375:20880:0:30:90:513:706:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:Jakubson (1988) described a two-step procedure for consistent estimation of  in labor 
14:376:20965:30:28:90:508:676:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:supply models. First, consistent estimates of the reduced-form parameters are obtained 
14:377:21051:28:30:90:520:648:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:from equation-by-equation estimation of (15), followed by identification of the structural 
14:378:21140:30:33:90:351:618:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:parameters , through minimum distance estimation: 
14:379:21189:33:28:90:525:585:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:F: 1ˆˆˆmin    (   )    ()(),DHH               (16) 
14:380:21246:28:33:90:514:557:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B: where  denotes the vector of structural parameters, ˆ is the vector of reduced-form 
14:381:21330:33:28:90:511:524:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:parameters obtained from the first step, ˆ is the variance-covariance matrix of ˆ, and 
14:382:21418:28:28:92:525:496:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:H is a design matrix that maps the structural parameters to the reduced-form parameters.  
14:383:21505:28:27:90:500:468:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:Where possible we confirmed the estimates of our nonlinear CRE models with linear 
14:384:21586:27:28:90:307:441:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:models containing individual fixed effects.    
14:385:21632:28:28:90:93:413:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B: 
14:386:21632:28:27:90:132:385:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:4. Data  
14:387:21639:27:28:90:502:358:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:To estimate our empirical models we used the 2004-2009 Medical Expenditure Panel 
14:388:21719:28:27:90:511:330:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:Survey (MEPS), subset to individuals aged 18-64 who were not full-time students. The 
14:389:21802:27:28:90:486:303:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:MEPS is a nationally representative overlapping panel survey designed to provide 
14:390:21880:28:28:90:502:275:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:estimates of health care use, expenditures, and health insurance coverage for the U.S. 
14:391:21966:28:27:90:503:247:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:civilian non-institutionalized population. The MEPS contains detailed information on 
14:392:22049:27:28:90:479:220:12:g_d0_f4:12:Times New Roman:B:respondents’ health status, demographic and socio-economic characteristics, and 
14:393:22129:28:27:90:483:192:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:employment information. Each panel of respondents was interviewed in 5 rounds 
14:394:22203:27:28:90:222:165:12:Times New Roman:11:Times New Roman:B:covering 2 calendar years.  
14:395:22228:28:28:126:505:137:11:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:A:     Our indicator variable for major depression was calculated using the Patient 
14:396:22308:28:27:90:515:109:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:Health Questionnaire (PHQ-2) index, collected during MEPS interview rounds 2 and 4.  
14:397:22391:27:0:90:508:82:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:The PHQ-2 is a validated screening tool for depressive disorders (Kroenke et al, 2003) 
15:398:22476:0:28:90:493:709:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:that is derived from two questions that ask whether the respondent was bothered by 
15:399:22558:28:28:90:501:681:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:"having little interest or pleasure in doing things" and whether he was "feeling down, 
15:400:22643:28:27:90:513:653:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:depressed and hopeless" during the past two weeks. For each question, respondents rate 
15:401:22730:27:28:90:498:626:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:themselves on scale of 0-3 based on the frequency of depressed mood and decreased 
15:402:22809:28:27:90:500:598:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:interest in usual activities. The PHQ-2 index is the sum of scores from the above two 
15:403:22894:27:28:90:514:571:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:items and ranges from 0-6. As suggested by Kroenke et al (2003), we coded individuals 
15:404:22975:28:28:90:515:543:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:as suffering from major depression if the value of the PHQ-2 index was greater or equal 
15:405:23056:28:27:90:499:515:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:to 3.6 Some respondents had missing values for the PHQ-2 index either because they 
15:406:23132:27:28:90:508:488:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:were ineligible for the Self-Administrated Questionnaire (SAQ) containing the PHQ-2 
15:407:23212:28:27:90:525:460:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:questions, or they did not respond to the SAQ.7 We excluded individuals ineligible for the 
15:408:23298:27:28:90:517:433:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:SAQ from our estimation sample, and for those where were eligible but did not respond, 
15:409:23384:28:28:90:428:405:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:we imputed a PHQ-2 index value using a generalized linear model.8    
15:410:23449:28:27:126:512:377:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:A:Respondents were asked to report on labor market outcomes in all 5 rounds, but 
15:411:23526:27:28:90:509:350:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:since the SAQ is only administrated in rounds 2 and 4 (in the middle of the each year), 
15:412:23610:28:27:90:489:322:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:we used the outcome variables collected during these same rounds. We considered 
15:413:23688:27:28:90:514:295:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:individuals with a current main job on the interview date as employed, but excluded the 
15:414:23771:28:52:90:524:267:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:self-employed from our estimation sample because the MEPS does not contain their wage 
15:415:23853:52:8:90:236:215:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:F:                                                           
15:416:23911:8:17:90:507:207:6:Times New Roman:10:Times New Roman:F:6 Kroenke et al (2003) found that PHQ-23 had a sensitivity of 83% and a specificity of 92% for major 
15:417:24012:17:9:90:139:190:10:Times New Roman:10:Times New Roman:F:depression.  
15:418:24024:9:18:90:506:181:6:Times New Roman:10:Times New Roman:F:7All adults above 18 as of the interview date were asked to fill out the SAQ, with the exception of those 
15:419:24130:18:13:90:518:163:10:Times New Roman:10:Times New Roman:F:made  ineligible because they were deceased, institutionalized, moved out of the U.S, or moved to military 
15:420:24237:13:9:90:131:150:10:Times New Roman:10:Times New Roman:F:facilities.  
15:421:24249:9:16:90:517:141:6:Times New Roman:10:Times New Roman:F:8 We used a GLM with a log link to account for the right skewness of the distribution of the PHQ-2 index. 
15:422:24354:16:11:90:503:125:10:Times New Roman:10:Times New Roman:F:In the imputation regressions, we included socio-demographic characteristics, the Physical Component 
15:423:24455:11:12:90:519:114:10:Times New Roman:10:Times New Roman:F:Summary (PCS) scores, and Mental Component Summary (MCS) scores. Both PCS and MCS scores were 
15:424:24549:12:11:90:503:102:10:Times New Roman:10:Times New Roman:F:calculated based on the questions in SF-12 Health Survey. The correlation between MCS score and the 
15:425:24649:11:12:90:518:91:10:Times New Roman:10:Times New Roman:F:PHQ-2 index is quite high (the correlation coefficient is -0.72, with the negative sign the result of opposite 
15:426:24760:12:0:90:180:79:10:Times New Roman:10:g_d0_f6:F:scaling on the MCS).  
16:427:24783:0:28:90:518:709:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:information.9 We converted hourly wage data and all monetary measures of productivity 
16:428:24866:28:28:90:339:681:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:costs to constant 2009 dollars using the urban CPI.  
16:429:24917:28:27:126:487:653:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:A:The MEPS question designed to measure workplace productivity loss asks 
16:430:24986:27:28:90:517:626:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:respondents "the number of times {the person} lost half-day or more from work because 
16:431:25071:28:27:90:480:598:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:of illness, injury, mental or emotional problems" during the interview round. We 
16:432:25150:27:28:90:516:571:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:constructed work loss days assuming that respondents lost a full day of work.  While we 
16:433:25237:28:28:90:488:543:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:believe this to be the most likely duration of work loss, it means that our estimates 
16:434:25323:28:27:90:521:515:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:represent the upper bound of the effect of depression on absenteeism. However, when we 
16:435:25408:27:28:90:524:488:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:computed aggregate productivity loss estimates from the work loss day models, we did so 
16:436:25493:28:27:90:514:460:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:assuming only half a day was lost to identify the lower bound, and a full day was lost to 
16:437:25582:27:28:90:497:433:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:identify the upper bound estimate. Due to the fact that the length of reference period 
16:438:25669:28:28:90:473:405:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:varies across respondents, we normalized work loss days to a 12-month period. 
16:439:25745:28:27:126:521:377:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:A:We controlled for a full set of socio-demographic and employment characteristics 
16:440:25824:27:28:90:505:350:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:in our models. Our main control variables include age and its square, gender, race and 
16:441:25907:28:27:90:496:322:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:ethnicity, marital status, region (Northeast, South, Midwest, West), urban residence, 
16:442:25988:27:28:90:502:295:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:years of education completed before entering the survey, union status,  employer size 
16:443:26071:28:28:90:513:267:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:(less than 25 employees, between 25-99 employees, between 100-500 employees, more 
16:444:26153:28:27:90:512:239:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:than 500 employees), benefits provided by the employer (sick pay, retirement plan, and 
16:445:26239:27:26:90:523:212:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:paid vacations), occupation and industry indicators,10 number of children under 5 or 18 in 
16:446:26325:26:8:90:236:186:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:F:                                                           
16:447:26383:8:18:90:516:178:6:Times New Roman:10:Times New Roman:F:9 Employed individuals who had missing hours or wage were dropped from the conditional sample. Those 
16:448:26483:18:13:90:508:160:10:Times New Roman:10:Times New Roman:F:who reported working more than 120 hours per week were also excluded due to concerns over reporting 
16:449:26583:13:13:90:519:147:10:Times New Roman:10:Times New Roman:F:error.  When estimating the aggregate cost of worker absenteeism due to depression we imputed the wages 
16:450:26687:13:9:90:337:134:10:Times New Roman:10:Times New Roman:F:of the self-employed and included them in our calculations.    
16:451:26748:9:18:90:508:125:6:Times New Roman:10:Times New Roman:F:10 The industry indicators include: 1. natural resources/mining/construction/manufacturing; 2. wholesale 
16:452:26852:18:13:90:503:107:10:Times New Roman:10:Times New Roman:F:and retail trade/transportation and utilities; 3. professional and business services/education, health, and 
16:453:26960:13:13:90:523:94:10:Times New Roman:10:Times New Roman:F:social services; 4. other services/public administration/military/unclassifiable industry. We also included an 
16:454:27071:13:0:90:396:81:10:Times New Roman:9:Times New Roman:F:indicator for whether the reported occupation required professional training. 
17:455:27150:0:28:90:519:709:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:the household, log of income earned by other family members (normalized by household 
17:456:27229:28:28:90:508:681:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:size), and year dummies. In order to control for physical health status, we included the 
17:457:27316:28:27:90:510:653:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:Physical Component Summary (PCS) score, which is derived from the questions in SF-
17:458:27396:27:28:90:510:626:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:12 Health Survey contained in the SAQ. Higher values of the PCS score indicate better 
17:459:27477:28:27:90:508:598:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:physical health status. In the regressions where the dependent variable is weekly hours 
17:460:27562:27:28:90:520:571:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:worked, we also included the log of hourly wages as a control to ensure our specification 
17:461:27644:28:28:90:518:543:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:is consistent with the standard labor supply model. Table 1 contains descriptive statistics 
17:462:27735:28:27:90:514:515:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:of all the variables we used in the analysis. Note that all means were weighted using the 
17:463:27822:27:28:90:509:488:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:MEPS SAQ weight which adjusts for SAQ non-response. In our estimation sample, 75 
17:464:27900:28:27:90:508:460:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:percent of all the individuals aged 18-64 were employed and 9.1 percent suffered from 
17:465:27981:27:27:90:181:433:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:major depression.  
17:466:27998:27:15:90:93:406:11:Times New Roman:11:Times New Roman:F: 
17:467:27998:15:27:90:142:391:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:5. Results 
17:468:28008:27:28:90:176:364:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:5.1 Employment  
17:469:28022:28:28:90:494:336:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:We report complete estimation results for the CRE probit models of employment in 
17:470:28101:28:27:90:506:308:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:columns (6) and (8), and the cross-sectional probit models for comparison purposes in 
17:471:28184:27:28:90:523:281:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:columns (2) and (4), of Table A1 in the Appendix. In all of our models, the random effect 
17:472:28270:28:27:90:523:253:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:capturing unobserved heterogeneity was specified to be correlated with marital status, log 
17:473:28359:27:28:90:486:226:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:of family income (excluding the individual's own income), the PCS score, and the 
17:474:28440:28:28:90:509:198:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:depression measure (index or indicator). Across all specifications, we found a negative 
17:475:28524:28:27:90:511:170:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:and statistically significant association between depression and employment. However, 
17:476:28610:27:28:90:494:143:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:the magnitude of the CRE estimates is substantially smaller than the cross-sectional 
17:477:28693:28:27:90:522:115:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:estimates for both the continuous PHQ-2 depression index and the dichotomous indicator 
17:478:28777:27:0:90:194:88:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:for index values ≥ 3.  
18:479:28799:0:28:126:527:709:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:A:The average marginal effects derived from these estimates are reported in Table 2.  
18:480:28882:28:28:90:515:681:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:The cross-sectional estimates imply that depression is associated with a 17.6 percentage 
18:481:28967:28:27:90:506:653:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:point reduction in the probability of employment, which is similar in magnitude to the 
18:482:29053:27:28:90:479:626:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:effect found in previous studies (Ettner et al, 1997; Alexandre and French, 2001; 
18:483:29134:28:27:90:481:598:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:Chatterji et al, 2011). In contrast, the CRE estimates imply depression lowers the 
18:484:29217:27:28:90:513:571:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:probability of employment by only 2.6 percentage points, or 3.5 percent. This is similar 
18:485:29301:28:28:90:505:543:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:to the marginal effect we obtain from a linear probability model containing individual 
18:486:29388:28:27:90:158:515:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:fixed effects.  
18:487:29403:27:28:126:496:488:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:A:The sizeable and significant correlation parameters in Table A1 indicate that 
18:488:29480:28:27:90:516:460:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:depression, along with marital status, physical health status, and income earned by other 
18:489:29568:27:28:90:473:433:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:family members, are endogenous in the reduced form estimating equation. This 
18:490:29644:28:28:90:523:405:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:endogeneity is presumably caused by the failure to fully measure worker productivity and 
18:491:29731:28:27:90:523:377:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:health status, which are captured by the random effect in the CRE model.  The downward 
18:492:29817:27:28:90:519:350:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:bias on the effect of depression on employment in the cross sectional model is consistent 
18:493:29905:28:27:90:482:322:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:with a positive correlation between unobserved productivity (or good health) and 
18:494:29984:27:28:90:465:295:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:employment, and a negative correlation between productivity and depression. 
18:495:30058:28:16:90:93:267:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B: 
18:496:30058:16:27:90:302:251:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B: 5.2 Hourly wage and weekly hours worked 
18:497:30096:27:28:90:522:224:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:Panel A of Table 3 contains marginal effects of depression on weekly work hours and the 
18:498:30181:28:28:90:517:196:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:hourly wage rate estimated using the conditional sample of workers. The cross-sectional 
18:499:30266:28:27:90:514:168:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:estimates imply that depression is associated with an 8.3 percent reduction in the hourly 
18:500:30355:27:28:90:510:141:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:wage, but this effect is small and imprecisely estimated using both CRE and individual 
18:501:30442:28:27:90:497:113:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:fixed effects to control for unmeasured productivity. We failed to find a relationship 
18:502:30528:27:0:90:506:86:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:between depression and weekly hours worked using either the cross-sectional or panel 
19:503:30615:0:28:90:480:709:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:data specifications. The correlation parameters from the CRE models reported in 
19:504:30694:28:28:90:510:681:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:appendix Table A2 indicate that the random effect is not correlated with the depression 
19:505:30781:28:27:90:521:653:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:measure in the work hours model, but that it is significantly correlated with depression in 
19:506:30872:27:28:90:503:626:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:the wage equation.11 The latter is consistent with the downward bias of depression on 
19:507:30956:28:27:90:521:598:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:wages due to unmeasured worker productivity in the cross sectional model. The marginal 
19:508:31043:27:28:90:503:571:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:effects from both cross-sectional and CRE ordered probit models for part-time versus 
19:509:31127:28:28:90:518:543:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:full-time employment are reported in panel B of Table 3. In the cross section, depression 
19:510:31216:28:27:90:497:515:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:reduces the probability of working full time by 1.5 percentage points while the CRE 
19:511:31298:27:28:90:466:488:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:estimates again suggest that depression has no effect on full-time work status. 
19:512:31375:28:27:90:96:460:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:  
19:513:31375:27:28:90:410:433:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:5.3 Absenteeism and aggregate productivity costs of depression     
19:514:31439:28:28:90:511:405:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:Unlike wages or hours, which are relatively rigid due to labor contracts, work loss days 
19:515:31527:28:27:90:518:377:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:are potentially more responsive to the presence or onset of contemporaneous depression. 
19:516:31612:27:28:90:482:350:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:We report the coefficient estimates of the ZIOP model in Table A4. Note that the 
19:517:31690:28:27:90:512:322:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:inflation part of the model captures the effect of depression on the propensity to be sick 
19:518:31779:27:28:90:516:295:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:enough to take days off, while the ordered probit part of the model captures the effect of 
19:519:31869:28:28:90:488:267:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:depression on the length of sick leave. The coefficient estimates from the inflation 
19:520:31952:28:27:90:522:239:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:equation indicate that the depressed are more likely to take days off from work in general 
19:521:32042:27:28:90:509:212:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:than are the non-depressed, although this effect is not precisely estimated. For both the 
19:522:32131:28:68:90:521:184:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:continuous and dichotomous measure, the coefficient estimates of the PHQ-2 indexes are 
19:523:32215:68:7:90:236:116:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:F:                                                           
19:524:32273:7:18:90:512:109:6:Times New Roman:10:Times New Roman:F:11 Note that the wage rate in the CRE work hours models is assumed to be endogenous, and as a result, is 
19:525:32377:18:0:90:288:91:10:Times New Roman:10:Times New Roman:F:specified to be correlated with the random effect. 
20:526:32429:0:28:90:483:709:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:positive and statistically significant in the ordered probit equation, indicating that 
20:527:32514:28:28:90:515:681:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:conditional on taking days off from work, depression increases the length of sick leave.  
20:528:32599:28:27:126:516:653:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:A:Marginal effects constructed from these coefficients are reported in Table 4. The 
20:529:32680:27:28:90:506:626:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:treatment effect specification suggests that depression increases work loss days by 1.4 
20:530:32767:28:27:90:518:598:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:days per year. This represents a one-third increase in work loss days relative to the mean 
20:531:32858:27:28:90:505:571:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:in the conditional sample of workers. Likewise, the marginal effect for the continuous 
20:532:32945:28:28:90:520:543:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:PHQ-2 index indicates that a one unit change in the index value increases work loss days 
20:533:33032:28:27:90:504:515:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:by 0.6 days per year. Although these are relatively large effects, the estimate from the 
20:534:33119:27:28:90:512:488:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:cross-sectional treatment effects model that fails to account for productivity differences 
20:535:33209:28:27:90:510:460:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:across workers is two and half times larger, while the estimate based on the continuous 
20:536:33295:27:28:90:238:433:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:index is nearly twice as large.  
20:537:33327:28:28:126:481:405:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:A:In addition, we examined whether depression has a differential impact on 
20:538:33398:28:27:90:506:377:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:absenteeism across worker groups. We stratified the sample by whether the individual 
20:539:33477:27:28:90:494:350:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:had a retirement plan as a proxy for salaried versus hourly paid jobs, and found that 
20:540:33558:28:27:90:488:322:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:depression is associated with a 43.3 percent increase in work loss days by workers 
20:541:33639:27:28:90:514:295:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:without retirement plans (hourly paid), and a 29.3 percent increase among workers with 
20:542:33722:28:28:90:514:267:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:retirement plans (salaried). Given that we controlled for whether the employer provided 
20:543:33806:28:27:90:523:239:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:sick leave or paid time off to visit medical care professionals, these estimates suggest that 
20:544:33899:27:28:90:360:212:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:the cost of depression is greater for lower paid workers. 
20:545:33956:28:27:96:488:184:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:A:        Using our CRE estimates of the impact of depression on work loss days and 
20:546:34038:27:28:90:513:157:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:information on the weekly work hours and wage rates, we were able to calculate annual 
20:547:34123:28:0:90:513:129:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:estimates of the aggregate cost of depression due to workplace absenteeism for the U.S. 
21:548:34212:0:28:90:518:709:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:working population.12 In Table 5 we report the aggregate cost from 2005-2008 using our 
21:549:34293:28:28:90:523:681:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:CRE estimates. Since the MEPS asks the respondents to report whether they missed work 
21:550:34374:28:27:90:505:653:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:for a half day or more due to sickness or injury, we calculated two different estimates: 
21:551:34462:27:28:90:511:626:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:Our upper bound estimate assumes individuals always missed a full day of work, while 
21:552:34547:28:27:90:497:598:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:our lower bound estimate assumes they always missed a half day. We found that the 
21:553:34627:27:28:90:513:571:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:annual total cost of workplace absenteeism due to depression is relatively constant over 
21:554:34715:28:28:90:362:543:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:time, and ranges from 0.7 to 1.4 billion in 2009 dollars.  
21:555:34768:28:27:90:96:515:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:  
21:556:34768:27:28:90:206:488:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:6. Sensitivity Analyses 
21:557:34791:28:27:90:519:460:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:We performed several sensitivity checks of our main results. First, we re-estimated all of 
21:558:34879:27:28:90:490:433:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:our models after excluding control variables for union status, industry, occupation, 
21:559:34962:28:28:90:519:405:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:employer size, and employer benefits (and wages). These variables could be endogenous 
21:560:35048:28:27:90:493:377:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:if those with depression seek employment only at firms with certain characteristics. 
21:561:35133:27:28:90:487:350:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:While the cross-sectional estimates of the impact of depression are sensitive to the 
21:562:35218:28:27:90:507:322:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:exclusion of these variables, the CRE estimates are not. Second, we tested whether the 
21:563:35303:27:28:90:504:295:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:differences between the cross-sectional and CRE estimates could be due to functional 
21:564:35387:28:28:90:513:267:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:form misspecification rather than unobservables. To address this, we re-estimated cross-
21:565:35473:28:27:90:514:239:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:sectional models after including quadratic and cubic terms of all continuous variables, a 
21:566:35562:27:40:90:524:212:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:full set of pairwise interaction terms, and lags of all the variables that were specified to be 
21:567:35656:40:7:90:236:172:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:F:                                                           
21:568:35714:7:18:90:512:165:6:Times New Roman:10:Times New Roman:F:12 For individuals who worked less than 70 hours per week, we assumed that they worked 5 days a week; 
21:569:35814:18:13:90:519:147:10:Times New Roman:10:Times New Roman:F:for those who worked more than 70 hours per week, we assumed that they worked 6 days a week. We then 
21:570:35915:13:14:90:512:134:10:Times New Roman:10:Times New Roman:F:calculated the daily wage by (weekly hours worked*hourly wage/number of days worked per week). The 
21:571:36013:14:13:90:524:120:10:Times New Roman:10:Times New Roman:F:total annual cost of depression is therefore the weighted sum of (daily wage*overall marginal effect) among 
21:572:36121:13:13:90:505:107:10:Times New Roman:10:Times New Roman:F:the depressed individuals. We imputed wages for the self-employed and included them in the aggregate 
21:573:36222:13:13:90:512:94:10:Times New Roman:10:Times New Roman:F:cost estimates. Since the 2003-2004 and 2009-2010 cohorts are excluded from the estimation sample, we 
21:574:36323:13:0:90:315:81:10:Times New Roman:10:Times New Roman:F:did not calculate the aggregate costs for 2004 and 2009. 
22:575:36381:0:28:90:473:709:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:correlated with unobserved heterogeneity in the CRE model.13 In the models of 
22:576:36457:28:28:90:518:681:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:employment and log hourly wage, the estimated effects of depression decreased after we 
22:577:36541:28:27:90:517:653:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:added the interaction and lag terms (see Table 6). However, the cross-sectional marginal 
22:578:36625:27:28:90:469:626:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:effects are still sizeable and precisely estimated even using this highly flexible 
22:579:36702:28:27:90:160:598:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:specification.  
22:580:36716:27:28:114:506:571:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:A:Third, we used a broader measure of mental illness, the Kessler-6 (K-6) index, to 
22:581:36794:28:28:90:508:543:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:investigate whether our results are sensitive to the scale we use to measure depression. 
22:582:36880:28:27:90:501:515:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:The K-6 index is a standardized and validated measure of non-specific psychological 
22:583:36964:27:28:90:512:488:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:distress, and reflects a diagnosis of anxiety disorder, or mood disorder, or non-affective 
22:584:37054:28:27:90:517:460:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:psychosis (Kessler et al, 2002). Individuals who scored greater or equal to 13 (out of 24) 
22:585:37144:27:28:90:521:433:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:are considered to have serious mental illness.14 We re-estimated all models using the K-6 
22:586:37231:28:28:90:522:405:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:index and report all the results in the Appendix. These estimates are consistent with those 
22:587:37321:28:27:90:490:377:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:from our primary specifications using the PHQ-2, and maintain the pattern of CRE 
22:588:37401:27:28:90:496:350:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:estimates of depression that are smaller than those from the cross-sectional models.  
22:589:37486:28:27:114:508:322:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:A:      Unfortunately, there is no direct way of assessing the robustness of panel data 
22:590:37571:27:28:90:499:295:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:techniques designed to account for unobserved heterogeneity without a confirmatory 
22:591:37654:28:28:90:504:267:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:randomized experiment or valid instrumental variables. However, one can assess how 
22:592:37736:28:27:90:497:239:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:sensitive the cross-sectional estimates are to selection on unobservables. If the cross-
22:593:37823:27:28:90:509:212:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:sectional estimates are very sensitive to unobservables, this provides strong motivation 
22:594:37911:28:38:90:521:184:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:for the CRE approach and suggests the estimates are likely to be more reliable. Using the 
22:595:37998:38:8:90:236:146:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:F:                                                           
22:596:38056:8:18:90:508:138:6:Times New Roman:10:Times New Roman:F:13 Since 2T for our panel, we only used the observations from the second year to include lags of time-
22:597:38157:18:8:90:519:120:10:Times New Roman:10:Times New Roman:F:varying controls. As a result, point estimates from baseline models differed from the full sample estimates. 
22:598:38264:8:18:90:502:112:6:Times New Roman:10:Times New Roman:F:14 In the MEPS, the K6 index was calculated based on questions that asked whether the respondent felt 
22:599:38365:18:13:90:523:94:10:Times New Roman:10:Times New Roman:F:"nervous", "hopeless", "fidget or restless"," worthless", "so sad that nothing could cheer the person up", and 
22:600:38476:13:0:90:289:81:10:Times New Roman:10:Times New Roman:F:"everything is an effort" during the past 30 days.  
23:601:38529:0:28:90:512:709:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:framework proposed by Altonji et al (2005) we determined whether a modest degree of 
23:602:38609:28:28:90:522:681:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:negative selection into depression on unobservables could account for the whole effect of 
23:603:38695:28:27:90:486:653:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:depression in the cross-sectional models. Other studies that have applied the same 
23:604:38776:27:28:90:527:626:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:framework include Altonji et al. (2008), Millimet et al. (2010), and Chatterji et al. (2011).  
23:605:38867:28:27:90:517:598:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:For example, Chatterji et al. (2011) demonstrated the utility of this method in measuring 
23:606:38956:27:28:90:510:571:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:associations between recent psychiatric disorders and the probability of employment; a 
23:607:39042:28:28:90:393:543:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:case where identifying instruments are not generally available. 
23:608:39105:28:27:126:507:515:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:A:Intuitively, the degree of selection on observables can be used as a guide to the 
23:609:39186:27:28:90:524:488:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:degree of selection on unobservables. In the case of binary outcome variable, consider the 
23:610:39277:28:28:90:252:460:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:following bivariate probit model:
