24:641:40429:33:30:90:488:508:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:cross-sectional estimate of , and setting  generates the lower bound of  
24:642:40505:30:30:90:503:478:12:Times New Roman:12:g_d0_f7:B:(Altonji et al, 2005). We followed a two-step procedure to approximate the value of 
24:643:40587:30:30:90:521:448:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:that satisfies equation (22). First,  and  are estimated from an unconstrained bivariate 
24:644:40672:30:30:90:479:418:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:probit model, and then  is estimated from a constrained bivariate probit model 
24:645:40748:30:32:90:359:388:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:imposing the estimated value of * from the first step.  
24:646:40801:32:29:114:513:356:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:A:     We set  from 0 to -0.4, * (-0.52 for our application) and */2 (-0.26), and 
24:647:40874:29:28:90:486:327:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:estimated the constrained bivariate probit models on employment. The coefficient 
24:648:40951:28:28:90:516:299:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:estimates and marginal effects of the dichotomous PHQ-2 index are reported in Table 7. 
24:649:41031:28:27:90:498:271:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:The negative effect of depression on employment decreases dramatically as negative 
24:650:41108:27:28:90:484:244:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:selection on the unobservables gets stronger. When ρ is set to -0.3, the coefficient 
24:651:41192:28:27:90:523:216:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:estimate becomes positive and the negative effect of depression goes away. This provides 
24:652:41281:27:28:90:519:189:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:evidence that the cross-sectional estimate is very sensitive to selection on unobservables, 
24:653:41372:28:28:90:492:161:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:and that even a modest level of negative selection on unobservables can reverse the 
24:654:41454:28:30:90:514:133:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:direction of the estimated effect. Under the assumption that selection along unmeasured 
24:655:41542:30:0:90:514:103:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:factors is equal to selection along measured factors (), the coefficient estimate is 
25:656:41633:0:28:90:506:708:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:positive and statistically significant. Under this condition the elements of X are just a 
25:657:41720:28:29:90:495:680:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:random subset of W, and are no more useful than the unobserved elements of W in 
25:658:41796:29:28:90:514:651:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:terms of reducing the bias in ˆ (Altonji et al, 2005). However, this assumption is likely 
25:659:41885:28:27:90:496:623:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:to be too strong given that our models contain a large number of socio-demographic 
25:660:41968:27:28:90:521:596:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:controls, some of which (such as education and age) are known to be strong determinants 
25:661:42056:28:28:90:171:568:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:of employment.  
25:662:42071:28:27:114:508:540:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:A:     Given the significant predictive power of the observables on employment, it is 
25:663:42151:27:28:90:507:513:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:reasonable to assume in our application that selection on unobservables is weaker than 
25:664:42237:28:30:90:491:485:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:selection on observables. The last column of table 7 contains the marginal effect of 
25:665:42321:30:30:90:500:455:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:depression on employment under the constraint: *0.5. In this case the marginal 
25:666:42402:30:28:90:496:425:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:effect is slightly smaller than that from our CRE model. Although it is impossible to 
25:667:42482:28:30:90:507:397:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:know the true value of , this suggests that the CRE specification generates estimates 
25:668:42567:30:27:90:443:367:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:that are consistent with a moderate degree of selection on unobservables. 
25:669:42639:27:28:126:521:340:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:A:In the case of continuous outcomes such as wages and hours worked, Altonji et al 
25:670:42720:28:28:90:494:312:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:(2005) provide a different method for assessing the role of unobservables. Here, the 
25:671:42803:28:27:90:522:284:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:relevant question is:  Relative to the degree of selection on observables, how large should 
25:672:42890:27:28:90:509:257:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:the selection on unobservables be, to explain away the whole effect of depression? We 
25:673:42973:28:27:90:498:229:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:provide a detailed derivation of statistic we used to determine this in section 2 of the 
25:674:43062:27:28:90:491:202:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:appendix. We conducted this sensitivity analysis only for the hourly wage outcome 
25:675:43140:28:28:90:507:174:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:because depression is not associated with hours worked in either the cross-sectional or 
25:676:43227:28:27:90:509:146:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:panel data model. Our estimates indicate that the normalized shift in the distribution of 
25:677:43316:27:28:90:474:119:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:unobservables only needs to be around 30 percent of the normalized shift in the 
25:678:43395:28:0:90:377:91:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:observables to explain away the entire effect of depression. 
26:679:43455:0:28:114:513:709:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:A: As a result, the OLS estimate suggesting that depression decreases wages is likely 
26:680:43537:28:28:90:508:681:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:less reliable than the CRE estimate indicating no effect. Although this exercise is not a 
26:681:43626:28:27:90:500:653:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:direct check of our CRE estimates, it is consistent with the significant differences we 
26:682:43713:27:28:90:497:626:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:observe between the cross-sectional and CRE models when worker productivity and 
26:683:43792:28:27:90:485:598:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:health status are not fully observable. If unobserved low productivity is positively 
26:684:43876:27:28:90:504:571:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:correlated with depression and negatively correlated with employment and wages, we 
26:685:43959:28:28:90:501:543:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:should find a smaller negative impact of depression on employment and wages in the 
26:686:44042:28:26:90:339:515:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:CRE models than the naïve cross-sectional models. 
26:687:44091:26:26:90:93:489:11:Times New Roman:11:Times New Roman:F: 
26:688:44091:26:27:90:246:463:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:7. Discussion and Conclusions 
26:689:44120:27:27:90:520:436:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:It is difficult to empirically evaluate the disabling effects of mental health conditions like 
26:690:44211:27:28:90:481:409:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:depression. The main challenge in estimation is the endogeneity of mental health 
26:691:44291:28:28:90:518:381:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:measures in the structural model. In this paper, we achieved identification by accounting 
26:692:44379:28:27:90:512:353:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:for time-invariant unobserved differences in productivity and health that are potentially 
26:693:44467:27:28:90:505:326:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:correlated with both labor market outcomes and depression. We found that depression 
26:694:44547:28:27:90:522:298:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:has a modest negative effect on employment and a large effect on absenteeism. However, 
26:695:44634:27:28:90:514:271:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:we did not find any causal effect of depression on wage or hours worked conditional on 
26:696:44717:28:28:90:156:243:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:employment. 
26:697:44728:28:27:90:515:215:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B: There are several limitations of our method. Although our identification strategy 
26:698:44808:27:28:90:507:188:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:is not dependent on exclusion restrictions, it hinges on the assumption that the way we 
26:699:44895:28:28:90:488:160:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:model unobserved heterogeneity fully accounts for the unobserved confounders of 
26:700:44973:28:27:90:522:132:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:depression. In all of our models, we specified the random effect in the structural model to 
26:701:45064:27:0:90:493:105:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:be correlated with marital status, income earned by other family members, physical 
27:702:45149:0:28:90:520:709:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:health status, and depression. This is reasonable if the main confounding factors are time-
27:703:45239:28:28:90:504:681:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:invariant unobserved productivity and unobserved dimensions of physical and mental 
27:704:45322:28:27:90:506:653:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:health status. We feel this is plausible in the case of health status since variation in the 
27:705:45413:27:28:90:499:626:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:PHQ-2 and PCS scores will capture time-varying dimensions of mental and physical 
27:706:45492:28:27:90:521:598:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:health, while age (conditional on educational attainment) should capture changes in labor 
27:707:45581:27:28:90:506:571:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:market experience, and as a result, time-varying productivity. Nonetheless, if the error 
27:708:45667:28:28:90:517:543:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:term has a time-varying component that is also correlated with depression, our estimates 
27:709:45755:28:27:90:165:515:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:will be biased.  
27:710:45770:27:28:126:488:488:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:A:Another limitation is that individuals with the most severe forms of mental 
27:711:45843:28:27:90:516:460:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:illnesses residing in institutions are not in the scope of the MEPS. One would expect the 
27:712:45932:27:28:90:493:433:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:effect of depression on employment to be larger for the full population. Finally, our 
27:713:46017:28:28:90:483:405:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:structural model captures the contemporaneous rather than the life-cycle effect of 
27:714:46099:28:27:90:496:377:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:depression. While a comprehensive assessment of the impact of depression on labor 
27:715:46180:27:28:90:514:350:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:market outcomes would consider both effects, the MEPS lacks information on the onset 
27:716:46265:28:27:90:377:322:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:and duration of depression necessary to estimate the latter.  
27:717:46323:27:28:114:498:295:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:A:    We found that depression has a smaller negative impact on employment than 
27:718:46401:28:28:90:505:267:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:previous studies. For example, Alexander and French (2001) reported a 19 percentage 
27:719:46485:28:27:90:514:239:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:point reduction in the probability of employment due to depression. Our cross-sectional 
27:720:46573:27:28:90:520:212:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:models produced a very similar estimate of 17.6 percentage points, but the CRE estimate 
27:721:46661:28:27:90:513:184:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:is only 2.6 percentage points. This could be due to the fact that we used data from 2004-
27:722:46749:27:28:90:505:157:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:2009, a time period during which the use of mental health care increased substantially 
27:723:46836:28:28:90:488:129:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:compared to the 1990s when the NCS was administered. Soni (2012) reported that 
27:724:46915:28:0:90:497:101:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:between 1999 and 2009, the number of adults treated for depression increased by 74 
28:725:47000:0:28:90:510:709:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:percent, and the total health care expenditures for depression increased from 18 to 22.8 
28:726:47089:28:28:90:511:681:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:billion in 2009 dollars. Given the effectiveness of depression treatment, this increase in 
28:727:47179:28:27:90:471:653:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:the use of mental health services might have dampened the disabling effects of 
28:728:47258:27:28:90:508:626:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:depression (Simon, 2002; Gibbons et al, 2012). Also, despite the fact that we found no 
28:729:47344:28:27:90:522:598:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:evidence of a causal relationship of depression on wage or hours, our aggregate estimates 
28:730:47433:27:28:90:436:571:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:of workplace productivity loss from short-term disability are not trivial. 
28:731:47506:28:28:126:512:543:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:A:In the aggregate, we found that the productivity loss in the U.S. economy due to 
28:732:47587:28:27:90:497:515:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:depression-induced absenteeism was between 700 million and 1.4 billion 2009 USD 
28:733:47666:27:28:90:475:488:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:annually, which is less than estimates from most previous studies. For example, 
28:734:47745:28:27:90:517:460:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:Greenberg et al. (2003) reported that the cost of depression from workplace absenteeism 
28:735:47829:27:28:90:489:433:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:totaled 36.2 billion in 2000 (current dollars). Birnbaum et al. (2010) estimated that 
28:736:47907:28:28:90:504:405:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:monthly depression-related productivity loss from both absenteeism and presenteeism 
28:737:47989:28:27:90:517:377:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:was 2 billion, also in 2000 dollars. Due to methodological differences, caution is needed 
28:738:48077:27:28:90:488:350:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:when comparing our estimates of aggregate costs with those from these studies. In 
28:739:48155:28:27:90:494:322:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:particular, we did not attempt to quantify the impact of depression on presenteeism, 
28:740:48240:27:28:90:506:295:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:which cannot be calculated using the MEPS without making an untestable assumption 
28:741:48319:28:28:90:463:267:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:about how depression lowers productivity at work. Previous studies may also 
28:742:48392:28:27:90:513:239:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:overestimate the workplace productivity loss due to absenteeism as a result of failure to 
28:743:48480:27:28:90:278:212:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:address the endogeneity of depression. 
28:744:48518:28:27:126:504:184:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:A:Our findings have implications, in particular, for the substantial expansions of 
28:745:48599:27:28:90:494:157:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:mental health coverage under the Affordable Care Act (ACA). Garfield et al (2011) 
28:746:48681:28:28:90:514:129:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:estimated that 2.0 million previously uninsured Americans with severe mental disorders 
28:747:48767:28:0:90:505:101:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:would gain coverage under the individual and small group exchange provisions of the 
29:748:48853:0:28:90:510:709:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:ACA.15  Mental health and substance use services are considered essential benefits and 
29:749:48940:28:28:90:499:681:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:must be covered at parity with other health services in the exchanges. In defining the 
29:750:49027:28:27:90:508:653:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:services as part of the essential benefit package, the government extends mental health 
29:751:49115:27:28:90:508:626:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:and substance abuse coverage well beyond the newly insured. The U.S. Department of 
29:752:49198:28:27:90:524:598:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:Health and Human Services estimates that 3.9 million Americans currently covered in the 
29:753:49286:27:28:90:493:571:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:individual market and 1.2 million currently in small group plans would gain mental 
29:754:49369:28:28:90:514:543:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:health coverage under the essential benefit requirement (Beronio et al, 2013).  A further 
29:755:49458:28:27:90:515:515:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:7.1 million currently insured Americans in the individual market and 23.3 million in the 
29:756:49546:27:28:90:519:488:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:small group market with some form of mental health coverage would now be guaranteed 
29:757:49630:28:27:90:517:460:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:parity coverage (Beronio et al, 2013). Our estimates suggest that some of these coverage 
29:758:49718:27:28:90:362:433:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:expansions may be offset through less productivity loss. 
29:759:49774:28:28:126:129:405:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:A: 
29:760:49774:28:27:126:129:377:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:A: 
29:761:49774:27:28:126:129:350:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:A: 
29:762:49774:28:27:126:129:322:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:A: 
29:763:49774:27:28:126:129:295:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:A: 
29:764:49774:28:28:126:129:267:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:A: 
29:765:49774:28:27:126:129:239:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:A: 
29:766:49774:27:28:126:129:212:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:A: 
29:767:49774:28:27:126:129:184:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:A: 
29:768:49774:27:41:126:129:157:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:A: 
29:769:49774:41:7:90:236:116:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:F:                                                           
29:770:49832:7:18:90:510:109:6:Times New Roman:10:Times New Roman:F:15 Garfield et al (2011) estimated that another 1.7 million Americans with severe mental disorders would 
29:771:49935:18:0:90:401:91:10:Times New Roman:10:Times New Roman:F:gain coverage under the Medicaid expansions if implemented in every state.
